Special Cases for the Agent: Substitutes, Offspring, and Consumption
Detailed furui' rulings on the limits of the agent's authority over substitutes, offspring, consumption, and redeposit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the limited authority of the wakil bi qabd al-ayn to complex scenarios involving substitutes, offspring, and consumption, using the Hanafi rules of qiyas and istihsan.

Core Idea
The agent for a specific item can only receive that item, not its substitutes or ancillary rights, except by istihsan in cases of consumption.

The previous lesson established the agent as a pure trustee. Now we apply that principle to a range of practical scenarios from Kafi al-Hakim. Can the agent collect compensation if the item is injured? What about offspring born before appointment, or fruit sold on the tree? The Hanafi school provides detailed guidance, often using qiyas but sometimes preferring istihsan. You will learn to distinguish between what the agent can and cannot take, and understand the reasoning behind each ruling.

Guided Path
1
Cases where the agent cannot take a substitute
Review the scenarios: (1) slave killed accidentally – agent cannot take blood money; (2) injury before receipt – agent takes slave but not compensation; (3) deposit hired out – agent does not take hire; (4) female slave copulated with by shubha – agent does not take dowry. In all these, the agent's authority is limited to the original item.
The analogy is to price (ثمن): these are considered substitutes or separate rights, not part of the item.
2
Cases where the agent can take additional items with the original
If the female slave or sheep gives birth after appointment, the agent takes the offspring with the mother. Similarly, fruit of the garden is treated like offspring. If the birth occurred before appointment, the agent cannot take the offspring.
Offspring and fruit are considered part of the deposit or item if they arise during the agency.
3
Consumption by the depositary: qiyas vs. istihsan
If the deposit is fungible (measured/weighed) and the depositary consumes it, then collects a substitute from the consumer, qiyas says the agent cannot take the substitute. But istihsan allows it, because the depositary is like a consumer and the agent should take the substitute as he would from the depositary.
The istihsan is based on fairness: the substitute replaces the original, so the agent should be able to take it.
4
Effect of principal's repossession
If the principal takes back the deposit and then redeposits it, or if the agent takes it and returns it, a new agency does not arise automatically. The agent cannot take it again unless reappointed. If he does take, the owner may hold either the agent or the depositary liable.
The agent's authority ends once the item leaves his possession with the principal's action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وبقبض العين ) أي الوكيل بقبض العين لا يكون وكيلاً بالخصومة لأنه أمين محض والقبض ليس بمبادلة فأشبه الرسول حتى إن من وكل وكيلاً بقبض عبد له فأقام ذو اليد البينة أن الموكل باعه إياه وقف الأمر حتى يحضر الغائب وهذا استحسان، والقياس أن يدفع إلى الوكيل لأن البينة قامت لا على الخصم فلم تعتبر وجه الاستحسان أنه خصم في قصر يده لقيامه مقام الموكل في القبض فتقصر يده حتى لو حضر البائع تعاد البينة على البيع وصار كما إذا أقام البينة على أن الموكل عزله عن ذلك فإنها تقبل في قصر يده كذا هذا، وكذا الإعتاق والطلاق وغير ذلك معناه إذا أقامت المرأة البينة على الطلاق والعبد أو الأمة على الإعتاق على الوكيل بنقلهم تقبل في قصر يدهم حتى يحضر الغائب استحساناً دون العتق والطلاق كما إذا ادعى ذو اليد الارتهان من الموكل وبرهن تقصر يد الوكيل عن القبض. وفي كافي الحاكم ولو وكل رجل عبد رجل بقبض وديعة له عنده مولاه أو عند غيره فباع المولى العبد أو أعتقه أو كانت أمة فولدت فالوكيل على وكالته وإذا وكله بقبض عبد له عند رجل فقتل العبد خطأ كان للمستودع أن يأخذ فيمته من العاقلة وليس للوكيل قبضها كالثمن، ولو قتل عند الوكيل كان له أخذها، ولو جنى على العبد قبل أن يقبضه الوكيل فأخذ المستودع أرشها فللوكيل أن يقبض العبد دون الأرش، وكذا لو كان المستودع أجره بإذن مولاه لم يأخذ الوكيل أجره، وكذلك مهر الأمة إذا وطئت بشبهة، ولو وكله بقبض أمة أو شاة فولدت كان للوكيل أن يقبض الولد مع الأم، ولو ولدت قبل أن يوكله بقبضها لم يكن له قبض الولد وثمرة البستان بمنزلة .الولد. ولو كان المستودع باع الثمرة في رؤوس النخل بأمر رب الأرض لم يكن للوكيل أن يقبضها وكذلك ولد الجارية إذا كانت الوديعة مما يكال أو يوزن فوكله بقبضها ثم استهلكها رجل فقبض المستودع من المستهلك مثلها لم يكن للوكيل أخذه قياساً، ولكن أستحسن أن يأخذه ولا أراه مثل قيمة العبد، أرأيت لو أكلها المستودع أما كان للوكيل أخذ مثلها منه؟ وإذا وكله بقبض وديعة ثم قبضها الموكل ثم أودعها ثانياً لم يكن للوكيل قبضها علم أو لم يعلم وكذا لو قبضها الوكيل ودفعها إلى الموكل ثم أودعها الموكل فإن قبضها فلرب المال تضمينه أو تضمين المودع ، فإن ضمن الوكيل لم يرجع على المودع، وإن
His statement: (And for receiving a specific item) i.e., the agent for receiving a specific item is not an agent for litigation because he is a pure trustee and receiving is not an exchange, so he resembles a messenger. So much so that if one appoints an agent to receive his slave, then the possessor establishes evidence that the principal sold it to him, the matter is stayed until the absentee appears. This is istihsan. Analogy would require that it be given to the agent because the evidence was not against the opponent, so it is not considered. The face of istihsan is that he is a contestant in shortening his possession because he stands in place of the principal in receiving, so his possession is shortened. So much so that if the seller appears, the evidence on the sale is retried. And it becomes like when he establishes evidence that the principal removed him from that; then it is accepted in shortening his possession. Similarly for manumission and divorce, etc. Meaning when the woman establishes evidence of divorce, and the slave or slave-girl establishes evidence of manumission against the agent, it is accepted in shortening their possession until the absentee appears, by istihsan, not regarding the manumission and divorce themselves. Similarly if the possessor claims pledge from the principal and proves it, the agent's possession over the item is shortened. In Kafi al-Hakim: If a man appoints another's slave to collect a deposit from his master or someone else, and the master sells the slave or manumits him, or if female and she gives birth, the agent remains on his agency. If he appoints him to collect a slave from a man, and the slave is killed accidentally, the depositary may take its value from the 'aqilah, and the agent has no right to collect it like the price. If it is killed with the agent, he may collect it. If injury occurs to the slave before the agent takes possession, and the depositary takes the compensation, the agent may take possession of the slave but not the compensation. Similarly if the depositary hired him with the master's permission, the agent does not take the hire. Likewise the dowry of a female slave if she is copulated with due to shubha. If he appoints him to collect a female slave or a sheep and she gives birth, the agent may take possession of the offspring with the mother. If she gave birth before he appointed him, he may not take the offspring. The fruit of the garden is analogous to the offspring. If the depositary sold the fruit on the palm trees by order of the landowner, the agent may not collect it. Similarly for the offspring of a slave-girl. If the deposit is of things weighed or measured, and he appointed him to collect it, then a man consumed it, and the depositary collected something similar from the consumer, the agent may not take it by analogy, but I istihsan that he takes it, and I do not see it like the value of the slave. Do you see that if the depositary consumed it, would the agent not take something similar from him? If he appointed him to collect a deposit, then the principal took possession of it, then deposited it again, the agent may not take possession of it, whether he knew or not. Similarly if the agent took possession and gave it to the principal, then the principal deposited it, then if he takes possession, the owner of the property has the option to hold the agent or the depositary liable. If the agent is held liable, he does not have recourse against the depositary...
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage explains the legal status of an agent appointed to receive a specific item (wakil bi qabd al-ayn). Unlike the agent for debt collection, he is a pure trustee (amin mahd) and not an agent for litigation. The key distinction is that receiving a specific item is not an exchange (mubadala), so he is like a messenger. The text then provides several scenarios: if the possessor of the item claims the principal sold it to him and produces evidence, the matter is stayed until the absent principal appears (istihsan); analogy would give the item to the agent, but istihsan delays. Similar rules apply for claims of manumission, divorce, or pledge. Then rulings from Kafi al-Hakim cover situations involving slaves, deposits, offspring, fruits, and substitutions. The agent's authority is limited to receiving the specific item; he does not have authority over other rights like blood money, hire, or compensation for injury. The passage also discusses cases where the deposit is consumed and the depositary takes a substitute—analogy denies the agent the right to take it, but istihsan allows it.

Key Terms
الوكيل بقبض العين (al-wakil bi qabd al-ayn): Agent appointed to receive a specific item (e.g., a slave, a deposit).
أمين محض (amin mahd): Pure trustee; one who is entrusted with property but has no authority to dispose of it or litigate.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; here used to allow the agent to take a substitute when the deposit is consumed, overriding qiyas.
القَبْض (al-qabd): Taking possession; the act of receiving physical control over the item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Cannot take the substitute by qiyas, but can by istihsan.
B) Can always take the substitute.
C) Cannot take the substitute under any circumstances.
D) Must wait for the principal to authorize.

Key Takeaway
The agent for a specific item is strictly limited to the item itself; offsprring after appointment is included, but substitutes and ancillary rights are excluded except where istihsan permits taking a fungible substitute.

Agent for Taking Possession Has No Litigation Authority
Ruling with istihsan proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that an agent for taking possession of a specific item is not an agent for litigation, and explain why istiḥsān overrides qiyās in this case.

Core Idea
Agent for qabḍ al-ʿayn is a pure trustee – cannot litigate, must suspend third-party claims.

This lesson examines a key limitation in Hanafi agency law: an agent appointed solely to take possession of a specific item (like a slave) does not automatically gain authority to litigate disputes over that item. The commentator presents a scenario where a third party claims ownership, and explains why istiḥsān (juristic preference) demands suspension pending the principal's appearance, even though qiyās would hand the item to the agent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Agent's Limited Mandate
Recognize that the agent is appointed only to take possession (qabḍ al-ʿayn). He is a pure trustee (amīn maḥḍ), not a representative for litigation.
The agent resembles a messenger (rasūl), not a fully empowered agent.
2
Contrast Qiyās and Istiḥsān
Under qiyās, since the third party's evidence was not presented against the agent as a litigant, the agent should take the item. Under istiḥsān, the agent is effectively a litigant regarding possession removal, so the hand is suspended.
Istiḥsān considers the agent's practical role as a stand-in for possession.
3
Apply to the Slave Example
Analyze the case: agent sent to take a slave from a third party; third party proves principal sold him the slave. Istiḥsān: the matter is suspended until the principal returns.
The same ruling applies if the third party proves the principal dismissed the agent.
4
Extend to Analogous Cases
If a woman claims divorce or a slave claims emancipation against the agent, istiḥsān again suspends the agent's right to take possession. The agent's hand is temporarily removed.
This shows the pattern: any third-party claim that challenges the principal's right suspends the agent's possession authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وبقبض العين (لا أي الوكيل بقبض العين لا يكون وكيلاً بالخصومة لأنه أمين محض والقبض ليس بمبادلة فأشبه الرسول حتى إن من وكل وكيلاً بقبض عبد له فأقام ذو اليد البينة أن الموكل باعه إياه وقف الأمر حتى يحضر الغائب وهذا استحسان، والقياس أن يدفع إلى الوكيل لأن البينة قامت لا على الخصم فلم تعتبر وجه الاستحسان أنه خصم في قصر يده لقيامه مقام الموكل في القبض فتقصر يده حتى لو حضر البائع تعاد البينة على البيع وصار كما إذا أقام البينة على أن الموكل عزله عن ذلك فإنها تقبل في قصر يده كذا هذا، وكذا الإعتاق والطلاق وغير ذلك معناه إذا أقامت المرأة البينة على الطلاق والعبد أو الأمة على الإعتاق على الوكيل بنقلهم تقبل في قصر يدهم حتى يحضر الغائب استحساناً دون العتق والطلاق كما إذا ادعى ذو اليد الارتهان من الموكل وبرهن تقصر يد الوكيل عن القبض.
His statement: (And by taking possession of the specific item) no, meaning the agent for taking possession of a specific item is not an agent for litigation because he is a pure trustee, and taking possession is not an exchange, so he resembles a messenger. So much so that if a person appointed an agent to take possession of a slave of his, and the possessor of the slave presented evidence that the principal sold it to him, the matter is suspended until the absent principal appears. This is istihsan. The qiyas is that it should be handed over to the agent because the evidence was not presented against the opponent, so it is not considered. The reason for istihsan is that he is an opponent in terms of removing his hand, because he stands in the place of the principal in taking possession, so his hand is removed. So much so that if the seller appears, the evidence on the sale is re-presented. It becomes like the case where someone presents evidence that the principal dismissed him from that agency – it is accepted for removal of his hand. Likewise, emancipation and divorce and other similar matters. Its meaning: if a woman presents evidence of divorce, or a male or female slave presents evidence of emancipation, against the agent regarding their transfer, it is accepted for removal of their hand until the absent principal appears, by istihsan – not [by qiyas] regarding emancipation and divorce. Similarly, if the possessor claims pawn from the principal and produces evidence, the agent's hand is removed from taking possession.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the matn that an agent appointed solely to take possession of a specific item (عين) does not have authority for litigation. The commentator provides the legal reasoning: the agent is a mere trustee (أمين محض) and taking possession is not a transaction, so he is like a messenger. He then presents an example: if the agent is sent to take possession of a slave from a third party, and that third party claims that the principal already sold him the slave and produces evidence, the case is suspended until the principal returns. This is istihsan (juristic preference). The qiyas would be to hand the slave to the agent because the evidence was not presented against the agent as a litigant. But istihsan prevails because the agent is effectively a litigant regarding the removal of his possessory right, as he stands in the place of the principal for taking possession. Therefore, his right to take possession is suspended until the principal can respond. The same applies if the third party claims that the principal dismissed the agent, or in cases of divorce or emancipation claimed by the party in possession. In all these cases, the agent's hand is removed temporarily pending the principal's appearance.

Key Terms
وكيل بالخصومة (wakīl bi al-khuṣūmah): An agent authorized to conduct litigation on behalf of the principal.
قبض العين (qabḍ al-ʿayn): Taking physical possession of a specific, identifiable item (e.g., a slave, a deposit).
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a more suitable ruling.
أمين محض (amīn maḥḍ): A pure trustee who has no discretion or authority beyond the terms of the trust.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The agent takes possession immediately.
B) The agent can litigate to enforce possession.
C) The matter is suspended until the principal appears.
D) The agent is dismissed and the slave goes to the third party.

Key Takeaway
An agent for qabḍ al-ʿayn is not an agent for litigation; third-party claims suspend his right to take possession until the principal appears.

Scope of an Agent's Authority over Deposits: The Deposit and Its Natural Increases
Parsing limits of agency for deposit taking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify what an agent appointed to take possession of a deposit may properly take and distinguish between the deposit itself and separate compensation or income.

Core Idea
The agent takes the deposit and its post-agency offspring, but not pre-existing increases or compensation.

The Kafi al-Hakim presents a series of cases clarifying the boundaries of an agent's authority when appointed to take possession of a deposit. These rulings emphasize that the agent's right is limited to the deposited item and what naturally accrues to it after the agency, excluding separate compensation (arsh, hire, dower) and increases that existed before the agency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the deposit and the mandate
The agent is appointed solely to take possession of the deposited item. Note the type of deposit: slave, female slave, ewe, measured/weighed items, etc.
The agency is specific to the item, not to claims or compensation.
2
Distinguish the deposit from separate compensation
If the depositary has already taken compensation for injury (arsh), hire, or dower from the deposited property before the agent takes possession, the agent does not take that compensation—he takes only the original item.
Compensation is treated as a separate right belonging to the owner, not to the agent.
3
Timing of increases: after vs. before agency
Offspring born after the agency, or fruit that ripens after, are part of the deposit and can be taken by the agent. If born or ripened before, they are separate and not included.
The agent’s authority extends only to what is part of the deposit at the time of taking.
4
Apply the istihsan exception for fungibles
For measured or weighed items consumed by another, qiyas would deny the agent the right to take the equivalent, but istihsan allows it because the agent could have taken the equivalent if the depositary himself had consumed it.
Istihsan overrides strict analogy to preserve practicality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي كافي الحاكم ولو وكل رجل عبد رجل بقبض وديعة له عنده مولاه أو عند غيره فباع المولى العبد أو أعتقه أو كانت أمة فولدت فالوكيل على وكالته وإذا وكله بقبض عبد له عند رجل فقتل العبد خطأ كان للمستودع أن يأخذ فيمته من العاقلة وليس للوكيل قبضها كالثمن، ولو قتل عند الوكيل كان له أخذها، ولو جنى على العبد قبل أن يقبضه الوكيل فأخذ المستودع أرشها فللوكيل أن يقبض العبد دون الأرش، وكذا لو كان المستودع أجره بإذن مولاه لم يأخذ الوكيل أجره، وكذلك مهر الأمة إذا وطئت بشبهة، ولو وكله بقبض أمة أو شاة فولدت كان للوكيل أن يقبض الولد مع الأم، ولو ولدت قبل أن يوكله بقبضها لم يكن له قبض الولد وثمرة البستان بمنزلة .الولد. ولو كان المستودع باع الثمرة في رؤوس النخل بأمر رب الأرض لم يكن للوكيل أن يقبضها وكذلك ولد الجارية إذا كانت الوديعة مما يكال أو يوزن فوكله بقبضها ثم استهلكها رجل فقبض المستودع من المستهلك مثلها لم يكن للوكيل أخذه قياساً، ولكن أستحسن أن يأخذه ولا أراه مثل قيمة العبد، أرأيت لو أكلها المستودع أما كان للوكيل أخذ مثلها منه؟ وإذا وكله بقبض وديعة ثم قبضها الموكل ثم أودعها ثانياً لم يكن للوكيل قبضها علم أو لم يعلم وكذا لو قبضها الوكيل ودفعها إلى الموكل ثم أودعها الموكل فإن قبضها فلرب المال تضمينه أو تضمين المودع ، فإن ضمن الوكيل لم يرجع على المودع، وإن ضمن المودع رجع على الوكيل وإذا وكله بقبضها اليوم فله قبضها غداً استحساناً، ولو قال اقبضها بمحضر فلان فقبضها في غيبته ،جاز، ولو أنكر ربها التوكيل وحلف وضمن المودع فله الرجوع على القابض إن كانت قائمة فإن ادعى الوكيل هلاكها أو الدفع إلى الموكل وقد ، صدقه المودع في الوكالة لم يرجع عليه، وإن كان كذبه أو لم يصدقه ولم يكذبه أو صدقه وضمنه المال كان له أن يضمنه ولو جعل للوكيل بقبض الوديعة أجراً جاز وعلى تقاضي الدين لا إلا أن يوقت ا هـ .
And in Kafi al-Hakim: If a man appoints an agent to take possession of a deposit belonging to him held by the agent's master or someone else, and the master sells the slave or emancipates him, or if the slave is a female and she gives birth, the agent remains on his agency. And if he appoints him to take possession of a slave of his held by a man, and the slave is accidentally killed, the depositary may take its value from the 'aqila, and the agent is not to take it like the price. If it is killed while in the agent's hand, he may take the value. If the slave is injured before the agent takes possession, and the depositary takes the compensation, the agent may take the slave but not the compensation. Similarly, if the depositary hired out the slave with the master's permission, the agent does not take the hire. Likewise, the dower of a female slave if she is cohabited with under a shubha. If he appointed him to take possession of a female slave or a ewe, and it gave birth, the agent may take the offspring with the mother. If it gave birth before he appointed him to take possession, he may not take the offspring. The fruit of a garden is like the offspring. If the depositary sold the fruit while still on the palm trees by order of the landowner, the agent is not to take it. Likewise, the offspring of a slave girl. If the deposit is something measured or weighed, and he appointed him to take possession of it, then a person consumed it, and the depositary took its equivalent from the consumer, the agent is not to take it by qiyas, but I consider it istihsan that he take it, and I do not see it like the value of a slave. Do you not see that if the depositary consumed it, would the agent not take its equivalent from him? And if he appointed him to take possession of a deposit, then the principal took possession of it and then deposited it again, the agent is not to take possession of it, whether he knew or not. Similarly, if the agent took possession and returned it to the principal, and then the principal deposited it, and the agent took it, the owner of the property may hold either the agent or the depositary liable. If the agent is held liable, he does not seek recourse from the depositary. If the depositary is held liable, he may seek recourse from the agent. If he appointed him to take possession of it today, he may take it tomorrow by istihsan. If he said 'take it in the presence of so-and-so', and he took it in his absence, it is permissible. If the owner denied the agency and swore, and held the depositary liable, then the depositary may seek recourse from the taker if the thing is still extant. If the agent claims it perished or he gave it to the principal, and the depositary believed him regarding the agency, he does not seek recourse. If he disbelieved him, or neither believed nor disbelieved, or believed him but held him liable for the property, he may hold him liable. And if he stipulates an fee for the agent for taking possession of the deposit, it is permissible. But for receiving a debt, it is not except if a time is fixed. End quote.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage presents a collection of subsidiary rulings concerning an agent appointed to take possession of a deposit (وديعة). The rulings are derived from Kafi al-Hakim and other sources, and they specify the scope and limitations of the agent's authority. Key points: (1) If the depositary (the person holding the deposit) is a slave, and the master sells or emancipates him, the agency continues; the change in status does not affect the agent's right to take possession. (2) If the deposited item (a slave) is killed accidentally, the agent cannot take the blood money (value) from the 'aqila; only the depositary can. But if the slave is killed in the agent's hand, the agent may take the value. (3) If the slave is injured before the agent takes possession, the agent takes the slave but not the compensation already taken by the depositary. (4) The agent does not take hire or dower that accrued from the deposited property before possession. (5) If the deposited item gives birth (offspring) after the agency, the agent takes the offspring with the mother; if before, he does not. Fruit on trees is analogous. (6) If the depositary sells the fruit by order of the owner, the agent cannot take it. (7) For measured or weighed items, if the depositary takes compensation from a consumer, the agent cannot take it by qiyas, but istihsan permits it because the agent could have taken the equivalent if the depositary himself consumed it. (8) If the principal retakes possession and redeposits, or the agent returns it and then the principal redeposits, the agent cannot take it again; if he does, the owner may hold either the agent or the depositary liable. (9) The agent may take the deposit on a later day than specified, and taking in the absence of a named witness is valid. (10) If the owner denies the agency and holds the depositary liable, the depositary may seek recourse from the agent if the deposit is still extant; if the agent claims it perished or was returned and the depositary believes him, no recourse. If the depositary disbelieves or is uncertain, he may hold the agent liable. (11) An agent may be paid for taking a deposit, but not for receiving a debt unless a time is fixed.

Key Terms
وديعة (wadīʿah): A deposit; an item left with a person for safekeeping without compensation.
مستودع (mustawdaʿ): The depositary; the person with whom the deposit is held.
أرش (arsh): Compensation for injury or damage to property; damages.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The ewe, the lamb, and the wool payment.
B) The ewe and the lamb, but not the wool payment.
C) Only the ewe, not the lamb or wool payment.
D) Only the wool payment, because it is income.

Key Takeaway
An agent appointed to take possession of a deposit takes the item and its post-agency natural increases, but not separate compensation or pre-agency increases.

Validity of Agent's Acknowledgment in Litigation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agent's acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the validity of an agent's acknowledgment in litigation, explain the qiyas and istihsan arguments, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
An agent's acknowledgment in litigation is valid only in court; outside court it is invalid and the agency ends.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the acknowledgment (iqrār) of an agent appointed for litigation (wakīl bil-khuṣūmah). The central question is whether such an acknowledgment binds the principal only when made in court or in any setting. We will explore the qiyas argument that invalidates it absolutely, the istihsan reasoning that restricts validity to the courtroom, and the variant positions of the early Hanafi masters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling from the matn
The matn states: the agent's acknowledgment is valid before the judge; otherwise (outside court) it is not valid. Start by fixing this baseline.
This is the ruling of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).
2
Map the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
List the four positions: Abu Hanifa & Muhammad (valid only in court), Abu Yusuf (valid absolutely), Zufar (invalid absolutely). Note who relies on qiyas vs istihsan.
The dispute is among the founders of the school.
3
Analyze the qiyas argument of Zufar
Zufar argues that acknowledgment is the opposite of litigation (conciliation vs. contestation), so the command to litigate excludes acknowledgment. This is pure qiyas.
Qiyas is the default, but istihsan may override.
4
Analyze the istihsan argument of the two
The two argue that the agency is valid and the agent's authority includes responding; acknowledgment is a valid response only in court because it metaphorically constitutes litigation there. Istihsan allows this context-dependent validity.
Istihsan is based on practical necessity.
5
Determine the tarjih and mufta bihi
The later authorities (Hidayah, Kifayah) adopt the position of the two. Thus, the mufta bihi is: acknowledgment is valid only in court; out-of-court acknowledgment invalidates the agency.
This is the relied-upon view for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو) أقر الوكيل بالخصومة عند القاضي صح وإلا (لا) أي وإن أقر على موكله عند غير القاضي لا يصح عندهما استحساناً وخرج به عن الوكالة، وصحح أبو يوسف إقراره مطلقاً، وأبطله زفر مطلقاً وهو القياس لكونه مأموراً بالخصومة وهي منازعة والإقرار ضدها لأنه مسالمة، فالأمر بالشيء لا يتناول ضده ولذا لا يملك الصلح والإبراء. وجه الاستحسان أن التوكيل صحيح وصحته تتناول ما يملك وذلك مطلق الجواب دون أحدهما عيناً فيصرف إليه تحرياً للصحة، فأبو يوسف يقول هو قائم مقام الموكل فلا يختص إقراره بمجلس القضاء، وهما يقولان إن التوكيل يتناول جواباً يسمى خصومة حقيقة إن أنكر أو مجازاً إن أقر، والإقرار في مجلس القضاء خصومة مجازاً لأنه خرج في مقابلة الخصومة أو لأنه له لأن الظاهر إتيانه بالمستحق وهو الجواب في مجلس القضاء فيختص به لكن إذا أقيمت البينة على إقراره في غير مجلس القضاء يخرج من الوكالة حتى لا يؤمر بدفع المال إليه لأنه صار مناقضاً وصار كالأب والوصي إذا أقرا في مجلس القضاء لا يصح ولا يدفع المال إليهما؛ كذا في الهداية. أطلقه وهو مقيد بغير الحد والقود فلا يصح إقرار الوكيل على موكله بهما للشبهة . وقيد بالخصومة لأن الوكيل بغيرها لا يصح إقراره مطلقاً، ومنه الوكيل بالصلح كما في كافي الحاكم كالوكيل بالخصومة لا يملك الصلح والصلح عقد من العقود فالوكيل بعقد لا يباشر عقداً آخر. وقيد بالتوكيل بالخصومة من غير استثناء لأنه لو وكله بها إلا الإقرار فعن أبي يوسف لا يصح وصححه محمد، وعنه أنه فصل بين الطالب والمطلوب فلم يصححه في المال فقال نعم تأمل قوله : وصار كالأب والوصي إذا أقر أي على اليتيم أنه استوفى حقه في مجلس القضاء لا يصح إقرارهما ولكن لا يدفع المال إليهما لزعمهما بطلان حق الأخذ. وإنما لا . إقرارهما لأن ولايتهما نظرية ولا نظر في الإقرار على الصغير، وأما التفويض من الموكل حصل مطلقاً غير مقيد بشرط النطر فيدخل تحته الإقرار والإنكار جميعاً غير أن الإقرار صحته تختص بمجلس القضاء على ما ذكرنا؛ كذا في الكفاية .
His statement: (And if) the agent in litigation acknowledges before the judge, it is valid; otherwise (no), meaning if he acknowledges on behalf of his principal before a non-judge, it is not valid according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) by istihsan, and he exits the agency. Abu Yusuf validates his acknowledgment absolutely. Zufar invalidates it absolutely, and that is the qiyas (analogy) because he is commanded to litigate, which is contestation, and acknowledgment is its opposite because it is conciliation. The command for something does not include its opposite, and therefore he does not have the right to settle or forgive. The reason for istihsan is that the agency is valid and its validity encompasses what he possesses, which is absolute response without specifying one of them in particular, so it is directed towards it in pursuit of validity. Abu Yusuf says: he stands in the place of the principal, so his acknowledgment is not restricted to the courtroom. The two say: the agency encompasses a response that is called litigation in reality if he denies, or metaphorically if he acknowledges. Acknowledgment in the courtroom is litigation metaphorically because it emerges in opposition to litigation, or because the apparent duty is to give what is due, and the response in the courtroom is specific to it. But if evidence is established of his acknowledgment outside the courtroom, he exits the agency so that the money is not ordered to be given to him, because he has become contradictory. He becomes like a father or executor who, if they acknowledge in the courtroom, it is not valid, and money is not given to them. So it is in al-Hidayah. It is unrestricted but restricted to other than hadd and qisas, so the agent's acknowledgment on behalf of his principal regarding these is not valid due to doubt. It is restricted to litigation because an agent for other than litigation, his acknowledgment is absolutely invalid. From this is the agent for settlement, as in Kafi al-Hakim: like the agent for litigation, he does not have the right to settle, and settlement is a contract among contracts, so an agent for a contract does not perform another contract. It is restricted to agency for litigation without exception, because if he appointed him for it except acknowledgment, then from Abu Yusuf it is not valid, and Muhammad corrected it. And from him (Abu Yusuf) that he distinguished between claimant and defendant, so he did not correct it regarding property, saying 'yes'. Ponder his statement: 'He becomes like a father and executor when they acknowledge' i.e., regarding the orphan that he received his right, in the courtroom, their acknowledgment is not valid, but money is not given to them due to their assumption that the right to take is void. The reason their acknowledgment is not valid is that their guardianship is based on consideration, and there is no consideration in acknowledgment against the minor. As for the delegation from the principal, it is absolute, not restricted by the condition of consideration, so it includes both acknowledgment and denial. However, the validity of acknowledgment is specific to the courtroom as we mentioned. So in al-Kifayah.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage addresses the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of an acknowledgment (إقرار) made by an agent appointed for litigation (وكيل بالخصومة). The base ruling from the matn is that if the agent acknowledges in court, it is valid; outside court, it is not valid. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two), based on istihsan. Abu Yusuf holds that the agent's acknowledgment is valid absolutely, whether in court or outside, because the agent stands in the place of the principal. Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl invalidates it absolutely, relying on qiyas: since litigation is contestation and acknowledgment is its opposite (conciliation), the command for litigation does not include its opposite. The Hanafi response is istihsan: the agency is valid and the agent is authorized to respond; acknowledgment is a type of response, and its validity is confined to the courtroom because the context of litigation requires that responses be made in court. The agent who acknowledges outside court is acting contrary to his mandate and becomes like a father or executor who acknowledges against a minor in court—such an acknowledgment is invalid. The rule is also restricted: it does not apply to hudud or qisas due to doubt, and it only applies to agency for litigation, not other types of agency. There is also a dispute within Abu Yusuf's own view: he distinguishes between the agent acknowledging in favor of a claimant or a defendant, and Muhammad corrects him. The practical fatwa relies on the position of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) that acknowledgment outside court is invalid and the agent exits the agency.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrār): Acknowledgment or confession by the agent on behalf of the principal in a legal claim.
خصومة (khuṣūmah): Litigation; the act of disputing or contesting in court.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that leads to a ruling different from qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, when is the acknowledgment of an agent appointed for litigation valid?
A) In any setting, as long as it is truthful.
B) Only in the presence of the principal.
C) Only in the courtroom (before the judge).
D) It is never valid because it contradicts litigation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi ruling is that an agent's acknowledgment in litigation is valid only if made in court; an out-of-court acknowledgment invalidates the agency and does not bind the principal.

Five Types of Agency for Litigation Based on Exceptions
Classifying the five types of agency for litigation based on exceptions to confession and denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the five types of agency for litigation (wakalah bi al-khusumah) based on the exception or inclusion of confession (iqrar) and denial (inkar), and identify the ruling for each type.

Core Idea
In agency for litigation, excluding confession or denial tailors the agent's authority; silence is always permitted.

The Hanafi jurists have analyzed agency for litigation in detail. The principal may wish to restrict the agent's powers, especially regarding confession, which can be binding. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq summarizes the five possible arrangements, drawing from earlier sources like al-Hidayah and al-Bazzaziyyah. Understanding these nuances is crucial for both the principal and the agent to ensure the agency serves its intended purpose.

Guided Path
1
List the five types
Read the passage and enumerate each of the five scenarios of agency for litigation.
Types are based on the presence or absence of authority to confess (iqrar) and deny (inkar).
2
Analyze the effect of each exception
For each type, determine what the agent is authorized to do: confess, deny, both, or only remain silent.
Silence (sukut) is always valid, even when both confession and denial are excluded.
3
Distinguish continuous vs. disjunctive stipulations
Note that the validity of an exception may depend on whether it is stated in the same session (mawsul) or separately (mafsul).
Continuous exceptions are generally valid; disjunctive ones may not be in the apparent narration.
4
Apply to a hypothetical scenario
Given a description of an agency contract, identify which type it falls under and the legal consequences.
Consider the principal's express words and whether the agent acts within authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة باب الوكالة بالخصومة والقبض
الثاني؛ كذا في الهداية وفي النهاية يصح استثناء الإقرار في ظاهر الرواية. وفي البزازية: ولو وكله بالخصومة غير جائز الإقرار صح ولم يصح الإقرار في الظاهر لو موصولاً. وفي الأقضية ومفصولاً أيضاً ولو وكله غير جائز الإنكار يصح عند محمد، ولو غير جائز الإقرار والإنكار قيل لا يصح الاستثناء لعدم بقاء فرد تحته وقيل يصح لبقاء السكوت ا هـ . فالحاصل أنها على خمسة أوجه كما في الذخيرة: الأول أن يوكله بالخصومة فيصير وكيلاً بهما. الثاني أن يستثني الإقرار فيكون وكيلاً بالإنكار فقط. الثالث عكسه فيصير وكيلاً بالإقرار فقط في ظاهر الرواية لأن الموكل ربما يضره الإنكار بأن كان المدعي به أمانة، ولو جحدها الوكيل يصح دعوى الرد بعده ويصح قبله ففيه فائدة الرابع أن يوكله بالخصومة جائز الإقرار فيكون وكيلاً بهما. الخامس أن يوكله بها غير جائز الإقرار والإنكار ففيه اختلاف المتأخرين الخلاصة: ولو كان التوكيل بسؤال الخصم واستثني الإقرار موصولاً صح وفي ومفصولا لا ا هـ. ويصح التوكيل بالإقرار ولا يصير به مقراً؛ كذا في النهاية. وفي منية المفتي: إذا استثنى إقراره فأقر خرج عن الوكالة . لا اهـ. قوله: (ولا يصير به مقراً) أي لا يصير الوكيل مقراً بقوله وكلتك أن تقر لفلان بكذا على وكتب الرملي أول كتاب الوكالة عند قول المؤلف وصح التوكيل بالإقراض والاستقراض» أقول: والتوكيل بالإقرار صحيح ولا يكون التوكيل به قبل الإقرار إقراراً من الموكل. وعن الطواويسي معناه أن يوكل بالخصومة ويقول خاصم فإذا رأيت لحوق مؤنة أو خوف عار علي فأقر بالمدعي يصح إقراره على الموكل؛ كذا في البزازية
Book of Agency, Chapter of Agency for Litigation and Collection. The second; as in al-Hidayah, and in al-Nihayah: the exclusion of confession is valid in the apparent narration. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: If he appoints him for litigation without [the power of] confession, it is valid, and the confession is not valid in the apparent [narration] if it is continuous. And in al-Aqḍiyah: also if disjunctive. And if he appoints him without the power of denial, it is valid according to Muhammad. And if without both confession and denial, it is said the exclusion is invalid because no individual remains under it, and it is said it is valid because silence remains. So the conclusion is that it has five aspects, as in al-Dhakhirah: First: that he appoints him for litigation, so he becomes agent for both. Second: that he excludes confession, so he becomes agent for denial only. Third: the opposite, so he becomes agent for confession only in the apparent narration, because the principal might be harmed by denial, as when the claim is a trust; if the agent denies it, the claim of return is valid after it and before it, so there is benefit. Fourth: that he appoints him for litigation with permission for confession, so he becomes agent for both. Fifth: that he appoints him without permission for confession and denial, and there is difference among later scholars. The conclusion: If the appointment is by request of the opponent and confession is excluded continuously, it is valid; and disjunctively, no. Agency for confession is valid, and by it he does not become a confessor; as in al-Nihayah. In Munyat al-Mufti: If he excludes his confession and he confesses, he leaves the agency. No. His statement: (And by it he does not become a confessor) meaning the agent does not become a confessor by his saying: I appointed you to confess for so-and-so with such-and-such, and al-Ramli wrote at the beginning of the Book of Agency at the author's statement: 'Agency for lending and borrowing is valid.' I say: Agency for confession is valid, and agency for it before confession is not a confession by the principal. And from al-Tawawisi: Its meaning is that he appoints him for litigation and says: Litigate, and when you see the incurring of expense or fear of disgrace upon me, then confess to the claim; his confession is valid against the principal; as in al-Bazzaziyyah.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the types of agency for litigation with respect to exceptions. The author, after citing earlier sources, summarizes five scenarios: (1) absolute agency for litigation, making the agent authorized for both confession and denial; (2) agency with confession excluded, so the agent may only deny; (3) agency with denial excluded, so the agent may only confess (in the apparent narration, because the principal might be harmed by denial, e.g., when the claim is a trust; if the agent denies, the principal can later claim return, so there is benefit in allowing confession); (4) agency with explicit permission for confession, so the agent is authorized for both; (5) agency without permission for either confession or denial, which leads to difference among later scholars—some say invalid because no act remains, others say valid because silence remains. The passage then discusses the ruling on agency for confession itself: it is valid, but the agent does not become a confessor simply by being appointed; confession must be made explicitly. If the principal excludes confession in the appointment and the agent confesses, he leaves the agency. The commentary also clarifies that if the agent is appointed for litigation and told to confess only upon certain conditions (like avoiding disgrace), the confession is valid against the principal.

Key Terms
الخصومة (al-khuṣūmah): Litigation; the legal proceedings in court including both claiming and defending.
الإقرار (al-iqrār): Confession or acknowledgment; admitting a claim against oneself in court.
الإنكار (al-inkār): Denial; refuting a claim in litigation.
الوكالة (al-wakālah): Agency; a contract whereby one person deputes another to perform a legal act on their behalf.
موصولاً (mawṣūlan): Continuously; in the context of agency, when the exception or condition is stated in the same session as the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) When the principal excludes denial

D) When the principal authorizes for litigation and explicitly permits confession

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi jurists classify agency for litigation into five types based on the scope of authority regarding confession and denial, with silence always permitted when both are excluded.

Invalidity of Agency of a Guarantor for Money and Validity of Agency for Self-Discharge
Ruling with proof: invalidity of agency of a kafil bil-mal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the agency of a kafil bil-mal is invalid and explain why, using the Hanafi condition that an agent must act for another, and distinguish it from the valid case of a debtor appointed to discharge himself.

Core Idea
An agent must act for another; a guarantor appointed to collect the guaranteed debt acts for himself, making the agency invalid.

Agency (wakalah) is a contract where one person appoints another to act on his behalf. But what happens if the person appointed to collect a debt is also personally liable for that same debt? The Hanafi school rules such an agency invalid because the 'agent' would be acting for himself, not for the principal. This lesson unpacks that ruling, examines the proof by analogy, and clarifies why a debtor appointed to discharge himself is valid—a subtle but critical distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the appointment of a kafil bil-mal (a guarantor for a debt) as an agent to collect that same debt from the original debtor. The ruling is that this agency is batil (invalid) from the outset.
2
Trace the reasoning (illah)
An agent must act for another (ghayr). If the kafil collects the debt, he discharges his own liability as guarantor; therefore he acts for himself. The agency is invalid because it lacks the essential condition that the agent works for the principal.
The acceptance of the agent's statement (that he collected) is normally trusted (amanah), but here it is not accepted because he benefits personally.
3
Examine the analogy (qiyas) with the freed slave
The text cites the case of a freed slave who is indebted to creditors. If the master (now freed) acts as agent to collect from the slave, it is invalid because collecting reduces the slave's debt, benefiting the master indirectly. The common illa is that the agent has a personal interest in the collection.
This analogy is from al-Hidayah and uses a clear parallel to illustrate the principle.
4
Answer the objection: debtor's self-discharge
One might object: 'A debtor appointed to discharge himself also acts for himself, yet that agency is valid.' The answer from Munyat al-Mufti: the debtor indeed acts for himself (relieving his liability), but he also acts for the creditor (dropping the debt). The condition is that the agent acts for another, not that he refrains from acting for himself. The dual benefit satisfies the condition.
Some commentators erroneously considered this a tamlik (transfer), but if it were tamlik, the creditor could not revoke before the act. Since he can revoke, it remains agency.
5
Apply to subsidiary cases
The text lists several related rulings: (a) Agency of a kafil bil-nafs (person) is valid; (b) Appointing an agent to collect from oneself or one's slave is invalid; (c) Assignor (muhil) cannot be agent of assignee (muhtal) to collect; (d) Debtor cannot be agent of the claimant's agent; (e) Guarantee for money invalidates agency even if it precedes or follows, because guarantee is stronger.
These cases reinforce the central principle and show its boundaries.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وبطل توكيل الكفيل بالمال لأن الوكيل من يعمل لغيره ولو صححناها صار عاملاً لنفسه في إبراء ذمته فانعدم الركن لأن قبول قوله ملازم للوكالة لكونه أميناً، ولو صححناها لا تقبل لكونه مبرئاً نفسه فيعدم الحسامية سبق توكيل المطلوب كما لا يخفى وإلى أن الوكيل بالبيع إذا كفل عن المشتري بثمن ما باعه لم تجز، وتجوز كفالة الوكيل بالقبض والوكيل بالنكاح بالمهر لاندفاع التنافي بصرف الحقوق عنه كما علم في His statement: (And the agency of the guarantor for money is invalid) because the agent is one who acts for another, but if we validate it, he becomes acting for himself in discharging his liability, so the pillar is lost, because the acceptance of his statement is concomitant with agency due to his being trustworthy; if we validate it, it is not accepted because he is discharging himself, so it ceases with the cessation of its concomitant. It is analogous to a slave who is in debt and his master frees him, so that he guarantees his value to the creditors and the slave is demanded for all the debt; if the claimant appoints him to collect the money from the slave, it is invalid, as we explained; thus in al-Hidayah. And an objection is raised: the agency of the debtor to discharge himself is valid, even though he acts for himself. The verification of its answer is what is in Munyat al-Mufti from his statement: If he appoints him to discharge himself, because even though he acts for himself by relieving his liability, he acts for the creditor by dropping his debt, and the condition for validity of agency is that he acts for another, not that he does not act for himself. As for the commentator's statement in his answer that it is a transfer (tamlik) and not agency, like his saying to his wife 'divorce yourself', it is an apparent mistake, because if it were a transfer, the creditor's revocation before he discharges himself would not be valid, while in fact it is valid. And in Talkhis al-Jami': If the creditor says to the debtor: 'I give the discharge to you' or 'discharge yourself' or 'make it lawful for yourself', and he says 'I have discharged' or 'I have made it lawful', he is discharged, because his word transfers to the commander, as in 'give this slave to yourself' and 'confess for Zaid against me' and 'divorce' and 'free' and everything that is done independently. In the claim of al-Bazzaziyyah from the section on discharge: If the agent does not attribute the discharge to the principal, it is not valid. And if the agency in the issue of the book is invalid and he collects from the debtor and it perishes in his hand, it does not perish on the claimant. And he indicated by its invalidity that if the claimant releases him from the guarantee, it does not become valid because it occurred invalid from the beginning, as if he guaranteed for an absent person, it is invalid; then if he is informed and he approves, it is not valid. And he qualified it with guarantee of money to indicate the validity of agency of the guarantor for a person. And the commentator qualified it with his appointing him for litigation, but it is not a qualification, because if he appoints him to collect from the debtor, it is valid. And the author indicated that if he appoints him to collect the debt from himself or from his slave, it is not valid, as in al-Khulasah; and that if the assignee (muhtal) appoints the assignor (muhil) to collect the debt from the person assigned (muhtal alayh), it is not valid, as in al-Nihayah; and to the invalidity of the debtor appointing the claimant's agent to collect, because in al-Qunyah: 'If he appoints him to collect his debt from so-and-so, and the debtor informs him, so he appoints him to sell his goods and pay its price to the creditor, so he sells it and takes the price, and it perishes, it perishes from the debtor's wealth, because it is impossible for him to be a payer and a receiver, and one cannot be agent for both the defendant and the claimant in payment and receipt.' And it is not contradicted by what is in al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyyah: 'If the debtor sends the debt with his agent, and he comes to the claimant and informs him, and he is pleased and says: Buy something for me, so he goes and buys something with part of it, and the rest perishes from him, some say: it perishes on the debtor. Some say: from the claimant's wealth. And this is more correct, because his order to buy is like his taking possession.' Because what is in al-Qunyah is when the claimant's agency preceded, and what is in al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyyah is when the defendant's agency preceded, as is not hidden. And to the fact that if the selling agent guarantees for the buyer the price of what he sold, it is not valid; but the guarantee of the agent for collection and the marriage agent for the dower is valid, because the conflict is removed by directing the rights away from him, as known in al-Talkhis. And if the guarantee of the agent for collection is valid, his agency becomes invalid, as in al-Mi'raj. And the conclusion is that the guarantee for money invalidates the agency, whether the guarantee precedes or follows, because it is stronger than agency.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage explains why the agency of a guarantor for money (kafil bil-mal) is invalid according to the Hanafi school, and clarifies that the agency of a debtor to discharge himself is valid, contrary to a mistaken objection. The core reasoning: an agent must act for another, not for himself. A kafil (guarantor) who is appointed to collect the debt from the debtor acts for himself because collecting the debt discharges his own liability as guarantor. Therefore, the agency is invalid from the start. The objection raised is: the agency of a debtor to discharge himself is valid even though he acts for himself. The answer, from Munyat al-Mufti, is that the debtor indeed acts for himself by relieving his liability, but more importantly he acts for the creditor by dropping the debt; the condition for validity is that the agent acts for another, not that he does not act for himself. The commentator who claimed this is a transfer (tamlik) rather than agency is mistaken; if it were a transfer, the creditor could not revoke before the act, but he can. The passage then discusses various subsidiary cases: agency of a guarantor for a person (kafil bin-nafs) is valid; appointment of an agent to collect from oneself or one's slave is invalid; appointment of the assignor to collect from the assignee is invalid; the debtor cannot appoint the claimant's agent to collect because it creates conflict of roles. Guarantee for money always invalidates agency because guarantee is stronger than agency.

Key Terms
الكفيل بالمال (al-kafil bil-māl): A guarantor who guarantees payment of a debt (surety for money).
إبراء الذمة (ibrā' al-dhimmah): Discharge of liability; freeing oneself or another from a debt.
تمليك (tamlīk): Transfer of ownership; making something owned by another.
الوكالة بالخصومة (al-wakālah bil-khuṣūmah): Agency for litigation; authorizing an agent to represent in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the agency of a kafil bil-mal invalid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the guarantor is not a trustworthy person
B) Because the agent acts for himself in discharging his liability
C) Because the principal did not give proper consent
D) Because the guarantor has no legal capacity

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the agency of a kafil bil-mal is invalid because the agent acts for himself, while the debtor's agency for self-discharge is valid because he also acts for the creditor — the condition is acting for another, not abstaining from self-benefit.

6 min
Invalidity of Debtor Appointing Creditor's Agent to Collect
Rulings on invalid agency for debt collection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify scenarios where an agency for debt collection is invalid due to conflict of interest, and apply the Hanafi ruling that one person cannot be agent for both parties.

Core Idea
One person cannot simultaneously act as agent for both debtor and creditor in the same transaction.

This lesson examines specific scenarios where an agency appointment for collecting a debt is invalid because the agent would represent both parties, creating a logical and legal contradiction. The key principle is that a single person cannot be both the payer and receiver in the same payment. We will explore three examples from the text and resolve an apparent contradiction between two Hanafi sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agency scenario
Read each scenario described in the passage: (1) agent appointed to collect debt from himself, (2) transferee appoints transferor to collect, (3) debtor appoints creditor's agent to sell goods for payment.
Focus on who appoints whom and what the agent is asked to do.
2
Determine if the agent represents both parties
In each scenario, ask: Is the agent acting for both the debtor and the creditor? If yes, the agency is invalid because it creates a conflict of interest.
The agent cannot simultaneously be the payer (qāḍin) and the receiver (muqtaḍin).
3
Apply the principle of impossibility
The Hanafi ruling is based on the logical impossibility of one person being both payer and receiver in the same transaction. If the agency is invalid, any possession by the agent is considered that of the debtor, so loss falls on the debtor.
This is a dalīl ʿaqlī (rational proof) supported by istiḥsān.
4
Distinguish the valid scenario from al-Wāqiʿāt al-Ḥusāmiyya
In that case, the debtor's own agent brings money to the creditor, who then asks him to buy something. Here the agent is only the debtor's agent, not the creditor's, so the agency is valid and loss after the creditor's instruction is on the creditor.
The key difference is whose agent initiated the transaction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار المؤلف إلى أنه لو وكله بقبض الدين من نفسه أو من عبده لم يصح كما الخلاصة، وإلى أن المحتال لو وكل المحيل بقبض الدين من المحال عليه لم يصح كما في النهاية، وإلى بطلان توكيل المديون وكيل الطالب بالقبض لما في القنية : ولو وكله بقبض دينه على فلان فأخبر به المديون فوكله ببيع سلعته وإيفاء ثمنه إلى رب الدين فباعها وأخذ الثمن وهلك يهلك من مال المديون لاستحالة أن يكون قاضياً ومقتضياً، والواحد لا يصلح يكون وكيلاً للمطلوب والطالب في القضاء والاقتضاء ا.هـ. ولا يخالفه ما في الواقعات الحسامية : المديون إذا بعث الدين على يد وكيله فجاء به إلى الطالب وأخبره ورضي به وقال اشتر لي شيئاً فذهب واشترى ببعضه شيئاً وهلك منه الباقي قال بعضهم : يهلك المديون. وقال بعضهم : من مال الطالب. وهذا أصح لأن أمره بالشراء بمنزلة قبضه ا هـ. لأن ما في القنية فيما إذا سبق توكيل الطالب وما في الواقعات الحسامية سبق توكيل المطلوب كما لا يخفى
And the author indicated that if he appointed him to collect the debt from himself or his slave, it is not valid, as in al-Khulasa; and that if the transferee (muhtal) appointed the transferor (muhil) to collect the debt from the transferee (muhal 'alayh), it is not valid, as in al-Nihaya; and to the invalidity of the debtor appointing the agent of the creditor for collection, according to what is in al-Qunyah: 'If someone appointed him to collect his debt from so-and-so, and the debtor informed him, then the debtor appointed him to sell his goods and pay the price to the creditor, and he sold them and took the price, and it was destroyed, it is destroyed from the debtor's property, because it is impossible for him to be both payer and receiver, and one person cannot be agent for both the debtor and the creditor in payment and collection.' And it is not contradicted by what is in al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyya: 'The debtor if he sent the debt via his agent, and he brought it to the creditor and informed him and he was pleased, and said: buy something for me, so he went and bought something with part of it and the remainder was destroyed; some said it is destroyed from the debtor, and some said from the creditor's property, and this is more correct because his order to buy is tantamount to collection.' Because what is in al-Qunyah is in the case where the creditor's agency preceded, and what is in al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyya is in the case where the debtor's agency preceded, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage discusses situations where an agency for debt collection is invalid due to conflict of interest. The author indicates three invalid appointments: 1) collecting from oneself or one's slave (because the agent cannot be both debtor and creditor), 2) the transferee appointing the transferor to collect (since the transferor is the original debtor and cannot also be the collector), and 3) the debtor appointing the creditor's agent to sell his goods and pay the debt (because the agent would be acting for both sides in the same transaction, which is impossible). The text from al-Qunyah explains that if such an agent takes the goods and they are destroyed, it is from the debtor's property because the agency was invalid. Then a potential contradiction from al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyya is resolved: in that case, the debtor's own agent brought the money to the creditor, and the creditor then asked him to buy something; the destruction after that purchase is from the creditor's property because his order to buy is like collection, and the agency here is the debtor's own, not a mixed agency. The key principle is that one person cannot simultaneously be the agent of both parties in a payment transaction.

Key Terms
قاضٍ (qāḍin): The one who pays; the debtor in this context.
مقتضٍ (muqtaḍin): The one who demands payment; the creditor in this context.
وكيل (wakīl): Agent; a person appointed to act on behalf of another.
حوالة (ḥawāla): Transfer of debt; a contract by which a debt is transferred from one debtor to another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a debtor appoints the creditor's agent to sell his goods and pay the debt, and the goods are destroyed while in the agent's hands, from whose property is the loss?
A) The debtor's property
B) The creditor's property
C) The agent's property
D) It is shared equally

Key Takeaway
A single person cannot be the agent of both the debtor and the creditor in the same debt collection transaction; any such appointment is invalid (bāṭil) and the loss from the agent's hands falls on the debtor.

Claiming to Be Agent of an Absent Creditor: Payment Risks and Recourse
Rulings when someone claims to be agent of absent creditor and debtor pays

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a debtor pays a person claiming to be the agent of an absent creditor, and apply the conditions that determine whether the debtor must pay again or can recover.

Core Idea
Paying a claimed agent is at the debtor's risk—the absent creditor can demand payment again if the agency is denied.

When someone claims to be an agent of an absent creditor to collect a debt, the debtor faces a dilemma. The Hanafi ruling carefully balances the debtor's need to fulfill his obligation with the risk of paying the wrong person. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the sequence: payment to the claimant is initially valid if the debtor verifies him, but if the absent creditor later denies the agency, the debtor must pay again—then he can recover from the claimant if the money remains. Understanding this chain of rights and liabilities is crucial for anyone involved in debt collection or agency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the text deals with a person who claims to be an agent of an absent creditor (ghā’ib) for collecting a debt. The key actors: claimant (alleged agent), debtor (gharīm), and absent creditor.
2
State the initial ruling
If the debtor verifies the claimant (believes him), the judge orders payment to him. Reason: the debtor has confessed against himself – he admits owing the debt and accepts the claimant's authority.
This is based on the debtor's own admission, not on proof of agency.
3
Analyze the consequence if the absent creditor denies
If the absent creditor later appears and denies the agency, the debtor must pay the debt again to the creditor, because the original payment was not validly authorized. The debtor's say (with oath) is accepted.
The original payment becomes void (fāsid) because the agent's authority was not proven.
4
Determine the debtor's recourse
If the payment already made is still in the agent's hands (or its substitute), the debtor can recover it from the agent. But if the agent has consumed it and claims destruction/payment to the principal, the agent must swear. If the money was lost (without negligence), the debtor has no recourse.
The debtor's verification made him 'wronged' (mazlūm) in the taking, and the wronged does not oppress others.
5
Consider the objection and answer
An objection: if one of two sons verifies the debtor's payment to their deceased father, and the other son contradicts, the contradictor can recover his share from the verifying son. The answer distinguishes: the verifying son confessed a debt against his father (which binds him), unlike the debtor who only verified agency.
This shows that the ruling turns on the nature of the admission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن ادعى أنه وكيل الغائب بقبض دينه فصدقه الغريم أمر بدفعه إليه لأنه أقر على نفسه لأن ما يقبضه خالص ماله وسيأتي في الكتاب حكم ما إذا ادعى الإيفاء وقد تقدم أن الوكيل بقبض الدين وكيل بالمبادلة والتمليك والتملك فلا إشكال في صحة التوكيل به، ما في الذخيرة من السؤال والجواب كما لا يخفى وقول الشارح «هذا سؤال حسن والجواب غير مخلص الخ غفلة عما قدمه والمراد بأمره جبره عليه كما في السراج الوهاج قوله : (فإن حضر الغائب فصدقه وإلا دفع إليه الغريم الدين ثانياً) لأنه لم يثبت الاستيفاء حيث أنكر ذلك والقول في ذلك قوله مع يمينه فيفسد الأداء إن لم يجز استيفاءه حال قيامه قوله : (ورجع به على الوكيل لو باقياً) أي رجع الدافع بما قبضه الوكيل إن كان باقياً في يده / لأنه ملكه وانقطع حق الطالب عنه. أطلقه في البقاء فشمل البقاء الحكمي بأن استهلكه الوكيل فإنه باق ببقاء بدله ولذا قال في الخلاصة : وإن استهلكه ضمن مثله فإن ادعى الوكيل هلاكه أو دفعه إلى الموكل حلفه على ذلك، وإن مات الموكل وورثه غريمه أو وهبه له وهو قائم في يد الوكيل أخذه منه في الوجوه كلها، وإن كان هالكاً ضمنه إلا إذا صدقه على الوكالة قوله : (وإن ضاع (لا أي ضاع المقبوض في يد الوكيل فلا رجوع عليه لأنه بتصديقه اعترف أنه محق في القبض وهو مظلوم في هذا الأخذ والمظلوم لا يظلم غيره، وأورد عليه أن أحد الابنين إذا صدق المديون في دعواه الإيفاء للميت وكذبه الآخر ورجع المكذب عليه بالنصف فإن للمديون الرجوع على المصدق بالنصف إن كان للميت تركة غير الدين مع في زعمه أن المكذب ظالم، وأجيب بأن الرجوع على المصدق لكونه أقر على أبيه بالدين
His saying: (And whoever claims that he is the agent of an absent person for collecting his debt, and the debtor verifies him, he is ordered to pay it to him, because he [the debtor] has confessed against himself, since what he collects is purely his [the debtor's] own property. And in the book will come the ruling if he claims payment. And it has preceded that the agent for collecting debt is an agent for exchange, ownership, and taking ownership, so there is no problem in the validity of the agency for that. What is in al-Dhakhira of question and answer is as not hidden. And the statement of the commentator 'This is a good question and the answer is not satisfactory etc.' is neglectful of what he presented. And the meaning of 'his order' is compulsion upon him as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. His saying: (If the absent person comes and verifies him [the agent], otherwise the debtor pays the debt a second time) because the payment is not proved since he [the absent] denies it, and the say in that is his say with his oath, so the payment becomes void if his collection was not valid at its time. His saying: (And he recovers it from the agent if it remains) meaning the payer recovers what the agent collected if it remains in his hand, because it is his property and the right of the claimant has ceased from him. He gave it absolutely regarding remaining, so it includes constructive remaining if the agent has consumed it, for it remains by the remaining of its substitute. Therefore it is said in al-Khulasa: And if he consumed it, he is liable for its equivalent. If the agent claims its destruction or that he paid it to the principal, he [the agent] is made to swear to that. And if the principal dies and his creditor inherits him or gives it to him as a gift while it is still in the agent's hand, he takes it from him in all cases. And if it is destroyed, he is liable for it unless he [the creditor] verifies him [the agent] regarding the agency. His saying: (And if it is lost [i.e., what was collected in the agent's hand], then no recourse) because by his verification he acknowledged that he [the agent] was right in collecting, and he [the debtor] is wronged in this taking, and the wronged does not wrong others. It was objected that if one of two sons verifies the debtor in his claim of payment to the deceased and the other contradicts him, and the contradictor recovers his half from the one who verified, then the debtor may recover his half from the one who verified if the deceased had other assets besides the debt, under the assumption that the contradictor is an oppressor. The answer is that the recovery from the one who verified is because he confessed a debt against his father.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where someone claims to be the agent of an absent creditor for collecting a debt. If the debtor verifies (believes) the claimant, the judge orders payment to him. This is because the debtor's confession is against his own interest; he acknowledges that he owes the debt and that this person is authorized to receive it. However, if the absent creditor later appears and denies the agency, the debtor must pay the debt again, because the original payment was not validly authorized. The debtor can then recover from the alleged agent if the collected amount still exists (or its substitute if consumed). But if the agent claims the money was destroyed or paid to the principal, the agent must swear to that. If the money was lost in the agent's hands without negligence, the debtor has no recourse because he voluntarily verified the agent. The passage ends with an objection and answer involving two sons and a deceased father: the distinction is that the son who verified the debtor did so by acknowledging a debt against his father, which is a different basis.

Key Terms
غائب (ghā’ib): An absent person, specifically the creditor who is not present.
غريم (gharīm): Debtor; the party who owes the debt.
استيفاء (istīfā’): Collection or receipt of payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a debtor pays someone who claims to be the agent of an absent creditor, and the absent creditor later denies the agency, what must the debtor do?
A) Pay the debt again to the absent creditor
B) Recover the payment from the false agent only if he admits fraud
C) The debtor is exempt because he paid in good faith
D) The debtor must swear that he did not know

Key Takeaway
The debtor must pay the absent creditor again if the claimed agent is not authorized, but can recover from the agent if the money remains.

12 min
Payment to a Claimant of Agency – Validity and Legal Analogy
Main ruling and legal analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a debtor pays an alleged agent based on confirmation, and explain the analogy that distinguishes agency to collect debt from agency to borrow.

Core Idea
Payment to an alleged agent is valid pending ratification; it is a message to borrow, not an agency to borrow.

When a person claims to be the agent of an absent creditor to collect a debt, and the debtor confirms this claim, the judge orders the debtor to pay. This payment is valid, but its finality depends on the absent principal's ratification. This lesson breaks down the ruling and the Hanafi legal reasoning that answers a key objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is the debtor paying a person who claims to be the agent of an absent creditor. The ruling: the judge orders payment because the debtor confessed against himself.
The payment is not final yet; it is conditional on ratification.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that such payment is valid (sahih) pending ratification. The agent is considered an agent for exchange (mubadala), which is valid in Hanafi law.
This is the position in zahir al-riwayah.
3
Locate the objection
An objection is raised: this agency seems like an agency to borrow (istiqrad), because debts are repaid with their equivalents, leading to set-off. Agency to borrow is invalid in Hanafi law.
This objection is mentioned in al-Dhakhira and by al-Zayla'i.
4
Follow the Hanafi response
The response distinguishes: this is a message to borrow, not an agency to borrow. The agent must attribute the collection to the principal, saying 'So-and-so appointed me to collect what he has against you.' The messenger in borrowing also attributes to the sender. Thus, it is valid as a message, not an agency.
The analogy is that both involve directing the debtor to give money, but the agent's attribution saves it from being an agency to borrow.
5
Identify the practical consequence
If the absent principal later confirms the agency, the payment stands. If he denies, the debtor must pay again and has recourse against the agent (as will be explained in the next lesson).
This sets up the recourse conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن ادعى أنه وكيل الغائب بقبض دينه فصدقه الغريم أمر بدفعه إليه لأنه أقر على نفسه لأن ما يقبضه خالص ماله وسيأتي في الكتاب حكم ما إذا ادعى الإيفاء وقد تقدم أن الوكيل بقبض الدين وكيل بالمبادلة والتمليك والتملك فلا إشكال في صحة التوكيل به، ما في الذخيرة من السؤال والجواب كما لا يخفى وقول الشارح «هذا سؤال حسن والجواب غير مخلص الخ غفلة عما قدمه والمراد بأمره جبره عليه كما في السراج الوهاج قوله : (فإن حضر الغائب فصدقه وإلا دفع إليه الغريم الدين ثانياً) لأنه لم يثبت الاستيفاء حيث أنكر ذلك والقول في ذلك قوله مع يمينه فيفسد الأداء إن لم يجز استيفاءه حال قيامه قوله : (ورجع به على الوكيل لو باقياً) أي رجع الدافع بما قبضه الوكيل إن كان باقياً في يده / لأنه ملكه وانقطع حق الطالب عنه. أطلقه في البقاء فشمل البقاء الحكمي بأن استهلكه الوكيل فإنه باق ببقاء بدله ولذا قال في الخلاصة : وإن استهلكه ضمن مثله فإن ادعى الوكيل هلاكه أو دفعه إلى الموكل حلفه على ذلك، وإن مات الموكل وورثه غريمه أو وهبه له وهو قائم في يد الوكيل أخذه منه في الوجوه كلها، وإن كان هالكاً ضمنه إلا إذا صدقه على الوكالة قوله : (وإن ضاع (لا أي ضاع المقبوض في يد الوكيل فلا رجوع عليه لأنه بتصديقه اعترف أنه محق في القبض وهو مظلوم في هذا الأخذ والمظلوم لا يظلم غيره، وأورد عليه أن أحد الابنين إذا صدق المديون في دعواه الإيفاء للميت وكذبه الآخر ورجع المكذب عليه بالنصف فإن للمديون الرجوع على المصدق بالنصف إن كان للميت تركة غير الدين مع في زعمه أن المكذب ظالم، وأجيب بأن الرجوع على المصدق لكونه أقر على أبيه بالدين قوله : أنه صغاراً أما إذا كان فيهم كبير فادعى الوصي عليه بالوكالة عن الدائن لا يحتاج إلى إقامة وصي وهي واقعة الفتوى تأمل قول المصنف : (فصدقه الغريم قال الرملي احترز به عما إذا لم يصدقه بأن كذبه أو سكت كما سيصرح به هذا الشارح في شرح قوله أو لم يصدقه على الوكالة» قوله : (وبه سقط ما في الذخيرة من السؤال والجواب قال الزيلعي وفي المسألة نوع إشكال وهو أن التوكيل بقبض الدين توكيل بالاستقراض معنى لأن الديون تقضى بأمثالها فما قبضه رب الدين من المديون يصير مضموناً عليه وله على الغريم مثل ذلك فالتقيا قصاصاً والتوكيل بالاستقراض، لا يصح. والجواب أن التوكيل بقبض الدين رسالة بالاستقراض من حيث المعنى وليس بتوكيل بالاستقراض لأنه لا بد للوكيل بقبض الدين من إضافة القبض إلى موكله بأن يقول إن فلاناً وكلني بقبض ما له عليك من الدين ولا بد للرسول في الاستقراض من الإضافة إلى المرسل بأن يقول أرسلني إليك وقال لك أفرضني فصح ما ادعينا أن هذا رسالة معنى والرسالة بالاستقراض جائزة؛ هكذا ذكره في النهاية (PAGE_312) ۳۱۲ کتاب الوكالة باب الوكالة بالخصومة والقبض به على الوكيل لو باقياً وإن ضاع لا إلا إذا ضمنه عند الدفع أو لم يصدقه على الوكالة لأنه أخذه لأنه مني إلا إذا ضمنه عند الدفع لأن المأخوذ ثانياً مضمون عليه في زعمهما وهذه كفالة أضيفت إلى حالة القبض فتصح بمنزلة الكفالة بما ذاب له على فلان قالوا ويجوز في ضمنه التشديد والتخفيف، فمعنى التشديد أن يضمن الغريم الوكيل فالضمير المستتر عائد إلى الغريم، والبارز إلى الوكيل. ومعنى التخفيف أن يضمن الوكيل المال الذي أخذه، وصورته أن يقول الغريم للوكيل أنت وكيله لكن لا آمن أن يجحد الوكالة ويأخذ مني ثانياً ويصير ذلك ديناً عليه ظلماً فيضمن ذلك المأخوذ فيصح فالضمير المستتر عائد إلى الوكيل والبارز إلى المال. وما في النهاية من أنه عكس ما في التشديد سهو إذ يقتضي أن المستتر للوكيل والبارز للغريم وليس بصحيح، وإذا رجع البارز إلى المال فظاهر الكتاب أن المراد بالمال ما قبضه مرجع الضمير في ضاع وما قبله وليس بصحيح لأن ما في يد الوكيل أمانة لتصديقه على الوكالة فلا يجوز أن يضمنه إذ ضمان الأمانات باطل فتعين أن يكون المراد به ما يأخذه منه الدائن ثانياً، وظاهر الكتاب أن لا رجوع على الوكيل حالة الهلاك إلا إذا ضمن. وفي الخلاصة والبزازية إلا إذا كان الغريم قال أخاف إن حضر الدائن أن يكذبك فيها وضمنه أو قال مدعي الوكالة اقبض منك على أني أبرأتك من الدين كما إذا قال الأب للختن عند أخذ صداق بنته آخذ منك على أني أبرأتك من مهر بنتي فإن أخذت البنت من الختن الصداق رجع الختن على الأب كذا قوله : (أو لم يصدقه على الوكالة ودفعه إليه على ادعائه معطوف على ضمنه أي إذا لم يصدقه فإنه يرجع عليه لأنه إنما دفع له على رجاء الإجازة فإذا انقطع رجاؤه رجع عليه . أطلقه فشمل ما إذا سكت لأن الأصل فيه
